    <title>ORD - Bitcoin Ordinals Marketplace</title>
    <script nonce="6MKKrnIsu/vwjRBDM22GRw==">
      ;(function () {
        var preference = 'system'
        var valid = { system: true, dark: true, light: true }
        function parseThemePreference(rawValue) {
          try {
            var parsed = JSON.parse(rawValue)
            return typeof parsed === 'string' ? parsed : null
          } catch {
            return null
          }
        }
        try {
          var match = document.cookie.match(/(?:^|;\s*)os_theme=([^;]+)/)
          if (match) {
            var parsedCookie = parseThemePreference(decodeURIComponent(match[1]))
            if (valid[parsedCookie]) preference = parsedCookie
          } else {
            var stored = localStorage.getItem('os:theme')
            if (stored !== null) {
              var parsedStored = parseThemePreference(stored)
              if (valid[parsedStored]) preference = parsedStored
            }
          }
        } catch (error) {
          console.warn('theme preference bootstrap failed', error)
        }

        var resolved = preference
        if (preference === 'system') {
          resolved = window.matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: light)').matches ? 'light' : 'dark'
        }

        document.documentElement.dataset.theme = resolved
      })()
    </script>
    <link
      id="fa-css-preload"
      rel="preload"
      as="style"
      href="/vendor/fontawesome/6.5.1-2/css/all.min.css"
    />
    <script nonce="6MKKrnIsu/vwjRBDM22GRw==">
      ;(function () {
        var preload = document.getElementById('fa-css-preload')
        if (!preload) return

        function applyStylesheet() {
          if (preload.rel !== 'stylesheet') {
            preload.rel = 'stylesheet'
          }
        }

        function preloadHasLoaded() {
          if (preload.sheet) return true
          if (!window.performance || !window.performance.getEntriesByName) return false

          var entries = window.performance.getEntriesByName(preload.href)
          for (var index = 0; index < entries.length; index += 1) {
            if (entries[index].responseEnd > 0) return true
          }

          return false
        }

        if (!preload.relList || !preload.relList.supports || !preload.relList.supports('preload')) {
          applyStylesheet()
          return
        }

        preload.addEventListener('load', applyStylesheet, { once: true })

        if (preloadHasLoaded()) {
          applyStylesheet()
          return
        }

        window.setTimeout(function () {
          if (preloadHasLoaded()) applyStylesheet()
        }, 0)
        window.setTimeout(function () {
          if (preloadHasLoaded()) applyStylesheet()
        }, 1000)
        window.setTimeout(applyStylesheet, 3000)
      })()
    </script>

Floored, & Rejected: A Landscape Experiment by CRFTD",description:"This experiment explores the concept of rebirth.\n\nThe more I reflected on the idea, the more convinced I became that rebirth can only occur through death. Something can only be made new once a previous cycle has ended.\n\nThere was a season in my life when I hit rock bottom. I had cancer. My wife left me. Friends betrayed and abandoned me. I was forced to give up everything I owned, including my dog.\n\nThis was my death.\n\nThe experience changed me so completely that the man I once was died. Slowly, I was rebuilt. But first I had to descend into the depths of who I was, grieve what had been lost, and begin putting the pieces back together.\n\nDuring that process, I spent countless hours in nature. The quiet landscapes reflected the state of my soul. This collection features photographs captured during that journey.\n\nBut I wanted the concept of rebirth to extend beyond the imagery and into the blockchain itself.\n\nFor that reason, I chose to inscribe these works on satoshis that already contained cursed ordinals. They were broken. Rejected. Existing at the very bottom of the floor.\n\nThe photographs underwent a similar transformation. I processed them through a generative adversarial network (GAN), a machine learning system where competing neural networks generate and evaluate imagery. The process pulled each photograph between what was and what might be.\n\nThe resulting outputs were too refined and beautiful. So I broke them down further in Photoshop, reducing them to simpler forms and compositions. I wanted them to embody the emptiness that comes with starting over.\n\nThis collection is an attempt to take what already existed and give it new life. To take digital artifacts the blockchain deemed worthless, cursed, floored, and rejected, and through art, offer them the same thing I experienced: a chance to become something new.\n\nWhen minting,
